< Rating>
3<//Rating>
< text>
When Golden Gate Bakery is closed or the line is too long, I usually come here for my egg tart fixed. They open early at 7am.
Their egg tarts is not as buttery as the golden gate, but still one of the better one in Chinatown. The crust here is in-between the cookie or the flaky version, and not too thick. The tart is soft and tender, yet not too sweet.
They have the egg white or egg yolk (yellow one) version of the tarts. I personally like the egg yolk version better.

I also tried their bread this time, but it tasted very dry, not as soft as I expect. Not sure if it has been more than 1 or 2 days...

I used to like their Hong Kong style milk tea, but this time I am disappointed. It was not smooth, a bit bitter , and not enough condensed milk. Large for $4. Maybe I would pay a little more and get a Starbuck coffee next time.</text>

< review>
I went to TLC Auto because of the great google review ratings.

Cons:  I parked my car on the street.  Upon returning to pick my car up (I did not pay for service here) my car was in the exact same location.  My car seat had not moved (I am under 5' 2").  However, I was informed my car was pulled into the back and diagnosed (in the one hour they had my car).

I called ahead and was told not to wait for my car to be diagnosed.  It would be diagnosed in 2-3 days.  I offered to wait at a near by coffee shop and was told my car would not be seen within the day.  As I headed home they called me after an hour letting me know my Prius battery needs to be replaced.  (They are booking maintenance 2-3 weeks out).

I left multiple engine performance issues written down (& left historical maintenance) and asked if other issues were looked at.  I was told no, the only issue is the hybrid battery.  TLC Auto wanted $115 for this diagnosis (Auto zone told me the same issue for free).

Pros:  Contact Green Bean Battery (greenbeanbattery.com) and they will come to your house and replace your Hybrid battery.  They also take your old battery for you.  They were less than half of what TLC Auto repair quoted me for a hybrid battery (life time warranty & replacements).  Green Bean Battery is very professional, polite, and quick.< /review>

< review>
Fins or Tails is serving up top quality fish with tasty sauces over white or brown rice or green salad. The details of what goes on your fish and on top of your bowl are almost entirely customer driven, with just a couple of options that cost extra, or restrictions on how much is served. Their medium sized bowl generally leaves me full and happy for ten-spot, there is a large bowl for a few dollars more and a small for a couple less.

I'm not sensitive to any regional differences in what exactly define good "poke", but I am confident about identifying good quality raw seafood. They are serving fish equal in quality to most of the local sushi bars.< /review>

106488779790956869559< /UserId.>
<username>Katrina Gigliotti</username><date>1556135316800< /date><Rate>5<//Rate>< Review>
We LOVE this place. We're moving soon, and I'm going to miss it so much. I'll have to stop by here on visits to family!

We came across this place a year or so ago, and we love to recommend it.
The coffee is real coffee and DELICIOUS. The sandwiches....omg. The best BLT around. When I'm craving a good blt, this is where I get it from.
I love that they have so many desserts with fruit in them! I'm not a huge fan of chocolate, since most chocolate tastes heavily of chemicals.
We don't mind that they close early sometimes because they're not getting enough business to economically justify staying open. They closed their other location, but I REALLY hope they don't close this one. You don't find enough small, relaxed Mom and Pop Cafe-style places here in the Bay Area anymore. Everyone is trying too hard, offering the same things, with the same decor.
Seriously, give this place a real chance, don't let it die out. It's too good.< /Review>

<Time>1621638364404<//Time><gmapID>0x80c2bf391265d04f:0x61a13f0966697b2c<//gmapID><username>Cary Brown<//username><review>The intimate, Philippe Stack designed, Katsuya Hollywood is complex, expensive, and brilliantly eclectic.  The Sushi Chefs bring the confident skill that compliments the modern artistic environment. Their sashimi plate is gorgeous.

The large reception area is decorated in a geometric pattern of twelve, three foot (1m) tall, twelve inchs (30 cm) square solid, under-lit, clear plastic resin columns, embedded with white knives. It is a homage to the tool of the sushi chef.

Shannon, our hostess, led us to one of two dinning rooms. The dining area, hidden behind a curtain.  Parting the curtain you enter a darkened dining room, that has just enough soft lighting for a romantic effect. The large wall facing us is covered with a giant photo of a brightly lit, seductive woman's eyes. She is always watching.

Katsuya was awarded "Travel and Leisure's" award for best design. The chairs are oversized and well padded. The tables are large enough to be comfortable. As the room fills it can be difficult to hear your companion.

Yes, Katsuya is wheelchair accessible. However it not easy. Here's how it's done. First, one of your party steps up the entrance stairway and let's the reception desk know a guest in a wheelchair ( or handicap) requires access. You and the disabled guest travel North to Hollywood Boulevard, turn West (left) and move past the "Pie Hole Restaurant" to a small unmarked door. Here you will be greated and taken into Katsuya. It is worth the effort.

Kyle, our server, is knowledgeable and friendly. We were presented with two menus, conventional and vegan. The conventional menu is extensive. The
vegan menu is two-thirds shorter. We ordered from the vegan menu.

Our meal, consisting of vegan appetizers: vegetable sushi, crispy rice and avocado, and crispy, shaved brussel sprouts. Each was prepared with care and artistry. Katsuya has four kitchens.

Parking is difficult and expensive.<//review>< Rating>

<Date>1523513095021< /Date><Rate>4< /Rate><Review>Took a large party to Katsuya. The food is very delicious - especially the super soft steak, the seaweed salad, and the salmon. The drinks are well created also. The whole meal inclusive for 8 people was about $750, so you should expect to spend $70-$90/head.

One issue with the venue was the understaffing. The food came out very quickly and sporadically; however, there was one lady taking care of half the restaurant. It's not her fault at all, but she was assigned to 10+ tables, which included 50+ people. As a result, you get your drinks slowly, refills slower, and the experience is shot.

For over $100 gratuity, I'd expect a bit faster service. Again, this is no fault of the waitress as she hauled ass, but the restaurant needs to increase their staff, especially during dinner rushes prior to shows.

I'll go again at some point as I really like the food, but will refrain from hosting a client event here.</Review>< Pictures>

<Review>Had an amazing Sunday night at Katsuya! My second time at the chain, but first at that location. I stuck with some of my choices from my first katsuya experience, but branched out as well. The Miso Glazed Black Cod was amazing, as usual; My favorite meal whenever it's offered on a menu.  The baked crab hand roll was tender and delicious as well! For our new choices, the truffle ponzu ceviche had amazing flavor and a plethora of fish choices. Finally, we went with the rock shrimp tempura roll. A lot of tasty shrimp on top for perfection! It was the perfect amount of spicy for a non-spicy lover like myself.
Service was also good! Always attended to.

All in all, I would definitely make a trip to katsuya. And if you have the budget splurge on the hot and cold courses. The rolls are delicious, but you can get specialty rolls at almost Japanese sushi places!</Review>< Name>

<gmapID>0x80c2bf391265d04f:0x61a13f0966697b2c</gmapID><name>Steven Vong</name>< review>
This is one of those places where you only need to eat there once.

After all the hype (celebrity sightings) and hearing all of my friends talk about this place, my friend and I decided to eat here for DineLA week. We made reservations for Thursday night at 7:00 PM.

The location is cool near the middle of Hollywood, near the Pantages and other theatres, concealed in a corner of the Boulevard. There is no place to find cheap parking so we paid $10 for the valet (expensive).

The entrance of the restaurant looks pretty cool, it's all glass so you can see the bar and contemporary designed environment. There are a lot of homeless people near the stairs on the sidewalk though, which made it awkward waiting for the valet/ standing outside the restaurant.

The restaurant wasn't too busy (but it got busy later when only one big table was empty), music was playing loud and the bar was packed. We were both ready to order since we knew the menu but the waitress didn't take our order until 5 minutes later.

The appetizer came out a couple of minutes later. I had onion albacore, which was much more onion than albacore. It was flavorful, but tiny, which left me unsatisfied. My friend ordered crispy rice with spicy tuna which was really good. However, there were only two pieces so the portion was too tiny. Then again, it was DineLA price so I guess it was only a sample.

Anyways, a long time later we got our tonkatsu. The tray looked nice. The beef bits and mushroom were tender and delicious, though a little salty. The glaze made the whole dish really good.

Last we got ice cream mochi, a single piece cut in half with a few pieces of fruit and panna cotta. Nothing special.

In conclusion, the food was good (highlights being the crispy rice and beef) but nothing amazing, the environment was modern and mostly aesthetically pleasing, and the service was average (food took forever but the waiters actually refilled my water lol). The sushi was better than most, but for its price the experience was not worth it. Katsuya definitely doesn't live up to its hype and celebrities really need to get better taste if they keep coming here.

(Side note: The bathrooms are really cool but kinda creepy. The napkins are reallly really nice)< /review>
